<td style="line-height:1.3em;"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Single_player_video_game" title="Single player video game">Single-player</a></td>

<p><i><b>Shin Megami Tensei: Persona 3</b></i> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">ペルソナ3</span><span class="t_nihongo_comma" style="display:none">,</span> <i>Perusona Surī</i><sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint"><a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets"><span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">?</span></a></sup>)</span> is a <a href="/wiki/Role-playing_video_game" title="Role-playing video game">role-playing video game</a> developed by <a href="/wiki/Atlus" title="Atlus">Atlus</a>, and chronologically the fourth installment in the <i><a href="/wiki/Persona_(series)" title="Persona (series)">Persona</a></i> series, a subseries of the <i><a href="/wiki/Megami_Tensei" title="Megami Tensei">Megami Tensei</a></i> franchise. <i>Persona 3</i> was originally published in 2006 on the <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_2" title="PlayStation 2">PlayStation 2</a> by Atlus in Japan; the North American release of the game was delayed due to issues with the publication of the official art book. An add-on disc titled <i><a href="/wiki/Shin_Megami_Tensei:_Persona_3#Persona_3_FES" title="Shin Megami Tensei: Persona 3">Persona 3 FES</a></i>, containing a "director's cut" of the original game, as well as a new <a href="/wiki/Epilogue" title="Epilogue">epilogue</a>, was released alongside <i>Persona 3</i> in Japan in 2007, and in 2008 in other territories, with a re-release of <i>FES</i> on the <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_Network" title="PlayStation Network">PlayStation Network</a> in 2012.</p>
<p>In <i>Persona 3</i>, the player takes the role of a male high-school student who joins the Specialized Extracurricular Execution Squad (SEES), a group of students investigating the Dark Hour, a time period between one day and the next that few people are aware of. During the Dark Hour, the player enters Tartarus, a large tower containing Shadows, creatures that feed on the minds of humans. To fight the Shadows, each member of SEES is able to summon a Persona, a manifestation of a person's inner self. The game's most iconic feature is the method by which the members of SEES release their Personas: by firing a gun-like object called an Evoker at their head. In addition to the standard elements of role-playing games, <i>Persona 3</i> includes elements of <a href="/wiki/Simulation_video_game" title="Simulation video game">simulation games</a>, as the game's protagonist progresses day by day through a school year, making friends and forming relationships that improve the strength of his Personas in battle.</p>
<p>There are official soundtracks for <i>Persona 3</i>, <i>Persona 3 FES</i>, and <i>Persona 3 Portable</i>, as well as an <a href="/wiki/Arrangement" title="Arrangement">arrangement</a> album containing music from multiple games in the <i>Persona</i> series. Music from the game has also been performed live at two concerts dedicated to the <i>Persona</i> series. <i>Persona 3</i> has seen a manga adaption, multiple <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Radio_drama_in_Japan" title="Radio drama in Japan">radio dramas</a>. Critical reception of <i>Persona 3</i> was mainly positive; reviewers enjoyed the game's social elements, while some found its combat and environments repetitive. <i>Persona 3 FES'</i>s epilogue was said to give narrative closure to the original game, although it was criticized for not featuring the simulation aspect of <i>Persona 3</i>.</p>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_Portable" title="PlayStation Portable">PlayStation Portable</a> version of <i>Persona 3</i>, titled <i><a href="/wiki/Shin_Megami_Tensei:_Persona_3#Persona_3_Portable" title="Shin Megami Tensei: Persona 3">Persona 3 Portable</a></i> was released in Japan on November 1, 2009, and in North America on July 6, 2010. The <a href="/wiki/Video_game_remake" title="Video game remake">remake</a> adds the ability to play as a female protagonist, new story elements and music, and a new interface designed for the PSP. In 2008, an original non-canon anime set 10 years after the events of <i>Persona 3</i>, titled <i><a href="/wiki/Persona:_Trinity_Soul" title="Persona: Trinity Soul">Persona: Trinity Soul</a></i>, was released in Japan and later in North America. Two <a href="/wiki/Fighting_game" title="Fighting game">fighting games</a> that continued the storyline of select members of S.E.E.S., <i><a href="/wiki/Persona_4_Arena" title="Persona 4 Arena">Persona 4 Arena</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Persona_4_Arena_Ultimax" title="Persona 4 Arena Ultimax">Persona 4 Arena Ultimax</a></i>, were released in 2012 and 2013 respectively.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Gameplay">Gameplay</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shin_Megami_Tensei:_Persona_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Gameplay">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Persona3library.jpeg"><img alt="A teenage boy with blue hair sits at a desk in his school's library, studying. The dialogue box in the lower-third of the screen reads &quot;You managed to solve a difficult problem!&quot; The top-right area of the screen denotes that the date is June 8, the current time period is &quot;After School&quot;, and the moon is full." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="335" data-file-width="480" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/53/Persona3library.jpeg/200px-Persona3library.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/53/Persona3library.jpeg/300px-Persona3library.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/5/53/Persona3library.jpeg/400px-Persona3library.jpeg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Persona3library.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Protagonist gains academic skills by studying in the school library. The upper-right area of the screen indicates the current date, time period, and phase of the moon.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><i>Persona 3</i> combines elements of traditional role-playing games and <a href="/wiki/Simulation_video_game" title="Simulation video game">simulation games</a>. The game follows the protagonist character, balancing their daily life of going to school and building relationships with other people with fighting evil beings known as Shadows during the mysterious Dark Hour. Each day is divided up between various time zones, the most common of which are "After School/Daytime" and "Evening". With the exception of scripted events, such as plot progression or special events, the player is free to choose how each day is spent, with most activities causing time to pass on. The types of activities and characters that can be interacted with vary depending on the day of the week and time of day. Additionally, some activities are limited by the protagonist's three attributes; Academics, Charm, and Courage, which can be built by performing various activities or making certain correct choices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manual28_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-manual28-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manual25_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-manual25-10">[10]</a></sup> During the evening, players can choose to visit Tartarus, the game's main dungeon, where they can build their party's experience and gain new items. On the day of the full moon, players will participate in a boss battle in order to progress the story.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1UP-Persona_3_Preview_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-1UP-Persona_3_Preview-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Personas_and_Social_Links">Personas and Social Links</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shin_Megami_Tensei:_Persona_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Personas and Social Links">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The main element of the game are the Personas, various creatures and monsters which are associated with the <a href="/wiki/Major_Arcana" title="Major Arcana">Major Arcana</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Tarot" title="Tarot">Tarot</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gamespot-Persona_3_Review_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gamespot-Persona_3_Review-12">[12]</a></sup> Each Persona has its own set of strengths and weaknesses, and possess various abilities, ranging from offensive and support abilities, to passive abilities that support the character. Whereas each of the game's main characters has their own Persona, some of which change form as the story progresses, the protagonist is capable of wielding multiple Personas, which can be switched between during battles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manual2627_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-manual2627-13">[13]</a></sup> New Personas can be created by visiting the Velvet Room and fusing together multiple Personas, passing along certain moves from the Personas used. The Personas that a player can create are limited by the current level of the protagonist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manual2627_13-1"><a href="#cite_note-manual2627-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manual3839_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-manual3839-14">[14]</a></sup> Personas can also be obtained from Shuffle Time following battles, and previously obtained Personas can be summoned from the Persona Compendium for a fee.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manual3839_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-manual3839-14">[14]</a></sup> The Velvet Room additionally allows players to take on quests, such as retrieving certain items, in order to obtain a reward.</p>
<p>New to the series are Social Links, bonds that are formed with several of the game's characters, with each Social Link representing a specific Major Arcana. By spending time with these characters, these Social Links increase in rank. When creating a Persona of a particular Arcana, an experience bonus will be granted if that Arcana possesses a Social Link, with greater bonuses awarded depending on the rank. Performing certain activities or carrying a Persona of a respective Arcana can help bring a Social Link closer to increasing in Rank. Maxing out a Social Link gives players the ability to create specific Personas of each Arcana. Conversely, negative actions, such as incorrect dialogue choices or dating multiple characters, can result in a Reversed Social Link, which can prevent players from summoning Personas of that Arcana until fixed. In the worst-case scenario, a Reversed Social Link can break, effectively removing all Personas of that Arcana from the game.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tartarus_and_Combat">Tartarus and Combat</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shin_Megami_Tensei:_Persona_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Tartarus and Combat">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Persona3_battlescreen.jpg"><img alt="Four of the game's playable characters surround a group of three enemies. The camera is centered behind the Protagonist, who is wielding a sword. A wheel-shaped menu of icons in the lower-left corner of the screen indicate available battle commands." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="720" height="133" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/ed/Persona3_battlescreen.jpg/200px-Persona3_battlescreen.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/ed/Persona3_battlescreen.jpg/300px-Persona3_battlescreen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/ed/Persona3_battlescreen.jpg/400px-Persona3_battlescreen.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Persona3_battlescreen.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A typical battle in <i>Persona 3</i>. The portraits on the right-hand side of the screen indicate the status of the player's party.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Tartarus is the game's main dungeon, which can be visited during the evening, provided the conditions allow it (e.g. the absence of some characters may prevent the player from visiting Tartarus that night).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IGN-Persona_3_Review_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-IGN-Persona_3_Review-15">[15]</a></sup> The player may order the other party members to split up to explore the area, or automatically attack Shadows on sight. Players will eventually come across boss floors, in which the player must defeat powerful Shadows in order to continue their progress. Additionally, certain floors halt further progress through the tower until the story progresses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manual2021_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-manual2021-16">[16]</a></sup> Occasionally, innocent civilians will wander into Tartarus, winding up on certain floors. Rescuing these civilians safely before a full moon appears grants bonus rewards obtained from the police station. Spending too much time in Tartarus may cause characters to become "Tired" or "Sick", which can affect their performance during battle. Additionally, if the protagonist becomes Tired or Sick, some activities, such as studying at night, may be hampered. Players can recover their status by taking certain items, visiting the infirmary, or going to bed early.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manual2021_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-manual2021-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>Battle occurs when the player comes into contact with a Shadow roaming the floor, with the battle party consisting of whoever is in close proximity. Attacking the Shadow without being noticed will give the player an advantage, whilst the enemy gains an advantage if the player is attacked first.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manual22_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-manual22-17">[17]</a></sup> Battles use the "Press Turn" system, in which both allies and enemies take turns to attack using weapons, items, or Persona abilities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gamespot-Persona_3_Review_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gamespot-Persona_3_Review-12">[12]</a></sup> Using the Tactics option, the player can assign specific battle AI to each party member (in <i>Persona 3 Portable</i>, they may also choose to issue direct commands).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manual3132_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-manual3132-18">[18]</a></sup> Offensive attacks are divided into three physical types; Strike, Slash, and Pierce, and six elements; Fire, Ice, Electricity, Wind, Light, and Dark, attributes of which both Personas and Shadows may possess strengths and weaknesses against. Physical abilities use up HP whilst elemental and support magic use SP. By exploiting an enemy's weakness or performing a critical attack, characters can knock the opponent down, granting that character an extra turn, though enemies can also take advantage of an ally's weakness to gain an additional turn.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IGN-Persona_3_Review_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-IGN-Persona_3_Review-15">[15]</a></sup> If the player manages to knock all opponents down, they may be granted the opportunity to perform an All-Out Attack, in which all able party members assault the enemies for massive damage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gamespot-Persona_3_Review_12-2"><a href="#cite_note-Gamespot-Persona_3_Review-12">[12]</a></sup> Allies who lose all of their HP can be revived using revival items and abilities, but if the protagonist loses all of their HP, the game will end.</p>
<p>When a battle is won, players gain experience points which are divided amongst the party members. Earning enough experience allows Personas to increase in level, granting improved stats and new abilities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manual2627_13-2"><a href="#cite_note-manual2627-13">[13]</a></sup> Some Personas may also grant Skill Cards, which can be given to other Personas to teach them new abilities. Raising the protagonist's level will allow higher level Personas to be summoned in the Velvet Room, as well as allow the player to carry more Personas. At the end of certain battles, a minigame known as Shuffle Time may appear, in which players select a card from a set that is shuffled around. These can grant bonuses, such as additional experience points, cash, or restored health, or give the player new Personas. However, selecting a cursed card will cause an extremely powerful monster, Death, to appear on the current floor.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Plot">Plot</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shin_Megami_Tensei:_Persona_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Plot">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Setting">Setting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shin_Megami_Tensei:_Persona_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Setting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The story of <i>Persona 3</i> takes place in a 2009 CE Japanese city called Iwatodai <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">巖戸台</span><sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint"><a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets"><span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">?</span></a></sup>)</span>, built and funded by the Kirijo Corporation. Experiments carried out ten years ago created the Dark Hour, a period of time that exists between one day and the next.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manual0405_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-manual0405-19">[19]</a></sup> During this time, most people are <a href="/wiki/Shapeshifting" title="Shapeshifting">transmogrified</a> into coffins and are not aware of the Dark Hour; however, there is a select group of people who aren't.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manual0405_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-manual0405-19">[19]</a></sup> The Dark Hour bends reality; Gekkoukan High School, where most of the characters attend school during the day, becomes a huge labyrinthine tower called Tartarus, and beasts known as Shadows roam the area, preying on the minds of those still conscious.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IGN-Persona_3_Review_15-2"><a href="#cite_note-IGN-Persona_3_Review-15">[15]</a></sup> The Shadows leave their victims in near-catatonic states outside of the Dark Hour.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> To investigate and learn about the Dark Hour, Shadows, and Tartarus, the "Specialized Extracurricular Execution Squad", or SEES, was created. SEES is a group of high-schoolers capable of summoning beings known as Personas to combat Shadows.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IGN-Persona_3_Review_15-3"><a href="#cite_note-IGN-Persona_3_Review-15">[15]</a></sup> The <i>Persona 3</i> instruction manual describes Personas as being "a second soul that dwells deep within a person's heart. It is an entirely different personality that emerges when a person is confronted with something from outside his world."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manual0405_19-2"><a href="#cite_note-manual0405-19">[19]</a></sup> Persona-users usually summon their Persona by firing a gun-like object called an Evoker at their head.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1UP-Persona_3_Preview_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-1UP-Persona_3_Preview-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Characters">Characters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shin_Megami_Tensei:_Persona_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Characters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Persona_3_characters" title="List of Persona 3 characters">List of Persona 3 characters</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Protagonist_(Persona_3)" title="Protagonist (Persona 3)">main character of <i>Persona 3</i></a> is a silent protagonist, named by the player at the start of the game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> He is a teenage boy, orphaned as a child, returning to the city he grew up in ten years prior to attend Gekkoukan High School.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manual0405_19-3"><a href="#cite_note-manual0405-19">[19]</a></sup> After learning of his ability to summon a Persona, he joins SEES, which is composed of students at his school: Yukari Takeba, a popular, cheerful girl; Akihiko Sanada, a calm and collected senior who leads the school's boxing team; and Mitsuru Kirijo, the Student Council President and daughter of the head of the Kirijo Group, who provides backup during battle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manual0607_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-manual0607-22">[22]</a></sup> As the game progresses, SEES gains several new members: Junpei Iori, a class clown and the Protagonist's best friend;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manual0607_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-manual0607-22">[22]</a></sup> Fuuka Yamagishi, a shy girl who replaces Mitsuru as a support character; Aigis, a female <a href="/wiki/Android_(robot)" title="Android (robot)">android</a> designed by the Kirijo Group to fight Shadows;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> Ken Amada, a middle schooler whose mother was killed by a Persona-user;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup> Shinjiro Aragaki, a former member of SEES who quit due to past events;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> and Koromaru, a dog capable of summoning a Persona.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Story">Story</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shin_Megami_Tensei:_Persona_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Story">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Persona 3 begins with the Protagonist transferring to Gekkoukan High School, and moving into a dorm in the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manual0405_19-4"><a href="#cite_note-manual0405-19">[19]</a></sup> After learning of his ability to summon a Persona, he is asked to join SEES, and is eventually elected its leader in combat. Additional members join SEES over time, all students attending Gekkoukan: Junpei, who had only recently discovered his ability to summon a Persona; Akihiko, whose arm injury prevented him from fighting; and Fuuka, who replaces Mitsuru as the team's support member. After awakening to his Persona ability, the Protagonist is transported to the Velvet Room, which its proprietor, Igor, says is a realm between "dream and reality".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> Igor explains to him that his Persona ability is special: he is the only member of SEES capable of wielding multiple Personas in battle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> In-game, the Velvet Room is where the player may fuse two or more Personas to create a new one. Igor also encourages the Protagonist to meet people and form bonds with them, known as Social Links. According to Igor, the power of his Social Links will determine his potential in combat.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>On nights when the moon is full, the city is attacked by a Shadow more powerful than the ones found in Tartarus. After several of these incidents, Mitsuru is forced to reveal to the team the origin of Tartarus and the Dark Hour. Ten years earlier, the Kirijo Group, a research company founded by Mitsuru's grandfather, began amassing and containing Shadows. They studied and performed experiments on them, in order to harness their power. However, the experiments went awry, allowing the Shadows to escape and assemble into twelve larger creatures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup> Each is affiliated with one of the twelve <a href="/wiki/Major_Arcana" title="Major Arcana">Major Arcana</a>. SEES's leader, Shuji Ikutsuki, informs them that, if they were to defeat all twelve of the greater Shadows, Tartarus and the Dark Hour would disappear forever.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>As the year continues, the group adds two more Persona-users to their team: Ken and Koromaru. While vacationing in <a href="/wiki/Yakushima" title="Yakushima">Yakushima</a>, Junpei, Akihiko, and the Protagonist encounter Aigis, who had recently escaped the laboratory where she was kept, despite having been deactivated for years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> For reasons she cannot explain, she has a need to be near the Protagonist, even breaking into his dorm room at night to monitor him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> Aigis is also enlisted in SEES. After defeating the twelfth and final Shadow, SEES learns that they had been misled by Shuji Ikutsuki. By destroying the greater Shadows, they have freed parts of a being known as Nyx, which will bring about the end of the world if it is fully restored.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Nyx, or the "maternal being", is the creator of Shadows; she is drawn to Earth by The Appriser, or "Death", a Shadow of the Death arcanum. SEES encounters The Appriser disguised as Ryoji Mochizuki, a recent transfer student to Gekkoukan High School.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Shadow experiments performed ten years earlier created the Death Shadow, albeit in an incomplete state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Aigis, unable to defeat the Shadow, sealed it inside the Protagonist, who was a child at the time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> By defeating the twelve greater Shadows, the Death Shadow was recreated. Its purpose is to usher Nyx into the world, who will bring about the extinction of the human race. Ryoji insists that Nyx cannot be defeated; however, he offers SEES an alternative. If they were to kill him, their memories of the Dark Hour and Tartarus would vanish, allowing them to continue life unaware of their impending death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Aigis, who now realizes why she wanted to protect the Protagonist, begins to believe that she is useless.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> She urges SEES to kill Ryoji, as they cannot defeat Nyx. Through encouragement from her friends, however, she gains the resolve to join with SEES as they attempt to fight Nyx.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<p>On December 31, <a href="/wiki/New_Year%27s_Eve" title="New Year's Eve">New Year's Eve</a>, the player must decide whether to kill Ryoji. If the protagonist kills him, the game cuts to Graduation Day, with the entirety of SEES (barring Aigis) losing their memories of the Dark Hour and the Shadows, ending on a dark note as they prepare to celebrate in blissful ignorance until Nyx inevitably brings about the fall. If he is spared, then the game continues, and on January 31, SEES ascends to the roof of Tartarus to face Ryoji, who has transformed into the Nyx Avatar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> While they are able to defeat him, Nyx continues to descend to Earth. As this is happening, the Protagonist is summoned to the Velvet Room, where Igor reminds him that the power of his Social Links would determine his potential. The Protagonist hears the voices of his friends encouraging him. The strength of his Social Links grants him the power of the "Universe", allowing him to seal away Nyx from humanity.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> The world returns to normal, though the memories of the past year related to the Dark Hour are lost to the members of SEES. However, Aigis and the Protagonist do remember. On Graduation Day, the two go to the roof of the school, where the members of SEES had promised to meet should they stop Nyx and live to see their graduation. As Mitsuru gives her graduation speech, she and the rest of SEES suddenly regain their memories, and the group rush to the roof to fulfill the promise they all made. It is here that Aigis thanks the Protagonist for giving her a purpose in life: protecting him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Development_and_design">Development and design</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shin_Megami_Tensei:_Persona_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Development and design">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Persona_3_AD.jpg"><img alt="Two male and one female student stand in a classroom.  Behind and above the Protagonist, who stands at the center, is the Persona Thantos, a humanoid demon with eight coffins attached to its body via chains." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="324" data-file-width="300" height="238" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/1e/Persona_3_AD.jpg/220px-Persona_3_AD.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/1/1e/Persona_3_AD.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Persona_3_AD.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A Japanese ad for <i>Persona 3</i>, created by the game's art director, Shigenori Soejima. The ad "contains three important game elements: school, Persona, and friendship."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><i>Persona 3</i> began development in 2004, after the completion of <i><a href="/wiki/Shin_Megami_Tensei:_Nocturne" title="Shin Megami Tensei: Nocturne">Shin Megami Tensei: Nocturne</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Shin_Megami_Tensei:_Digital_Devil_Saga" title="Shin Megami Tensei: Digital Devil Saga">Digital Devil Saga</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> In March 2006, the first details on <i>Persona 3</i> were unveiled in the Japanese gaming magazine <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Famits%C5%AB" title="Famitsū">Famitsū</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> In addition to announcing the game's Japanese release date of July 13, the three-page article detailed the game's premise, combat systems, and the Social Link system (known as "Community" in the Japanese version). It also profiled three characters—the Protagonist, Junpei, and Yukari—as well as their respective Personas: Orpheus, Hermes and Io.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>The main character artist and art director for <i>Persona 3</i> was <a href="/wiki/Shigenori_Soejima" title="Shigenori Soejima">Shigenori Soejima</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SoejimaInterview_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-SoejimaInterview-48">[48]</a></sup> Character artist for the previous <i>Persona</i> titles, <a href="/wiki/Kazuma_Kaneko" title="Kazuma Kaneko">Kazuma Kaneko</a>, gave the job to Soejima so he could gain more experience.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OtakuKaneko_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-OtakuKaneko-49">[49]</a></sup> Soejima felt a degree of pressure when designing the characters as he did not want to disappoint the series' fanbase. The goal was to make players of the <i>Megami Tensei</i> series feel gratified that they had supported the <i>Persona</i> series. In an interview, Soejima compared the game's aesthetic and style to a fantastical <a href="/wiki/Manga" title="Manga">manga</a>, citing its use of mecha-like Persona and Mitsuru's flamboyant styling. Soejima returned to design the character Metis for <i>FES</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SoejimaInterview_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-SoejimaInterview-48">[48]</a></sup> The anime cutscenes for <i>Persona 3</i> and <i>FES</i> were animated by animation production company Point Pictures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p>In an interview with the magazine <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Play_(US_magazine)" title="Play (US magazine)">Play</a></i>, lead director for <i>Persona 3</i> Katsura Hashino discussed why the decision was made to have party members be directed by an <a href="/wiki/Artificial_intelligence" title="Artificial intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>: "I think it's more fun to have the party members controlled by their AI, so each member's characteristics and personality are on vivid display. There were no objections raised among the Persona 3 development team, either." He also notes that the system "wasn't well received" by players of the game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> Later, the use of AI for the secondary party members was described as a stylistic choice representing the game's theme of conquering the fear of death through "bonds": each character was their own person, and the player could only influence things by interacting with them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> <i>Persona 3</i> does not include the negotiation elements of previous <i>Persona</i> or <i>Megami Tensei</i> games, which allowed players to talk to enemies during a battle to recruit them, earn money, or obtain items. However, the social elements of <i>Persona 3</i> (and its successor, <i><a href="/wiki/Shin_Megami_Tensei:_Persona_4" title="Shin Megami Tensei: Persona 4">Shin Megami Tensei: Persona 4</a></i>) are considered the equivalent of the negotiation system by the development team. Maragos said in a <a href="/wiki/1UP.com" title="1UP.com">1UP.com</a> interview that "negotiation isn't gone...And [it] still factors into Persona Fusion; it's still a big part of the game. I feel like it's disguised, but it's there."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1UP-p4localinterview_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-1UP-p4localinterview-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Localization">Localization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shin_Megami_Tensei:_Persona_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Localization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Language_localisation" title="Language localisation">localization</a> of <i>Persona 3</i> was handled by Yu Namba and Nich Maragos. During this process, the team worked to leave as much of the original Japanese content intact, continuing a trend started with <i><a href="/wiki/Persona_2:_Eternal_Punishment" title="Persona 2: Eternal Punishment">Persona 2: Eternal Punishment</a></i>. One of the ideas had by the team for <i>Persona 3</i> was to use it as a medium for introducing Japanese culture to a western audience.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DesPanel_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-DesPanel-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SMTnamba_55-0"><a href="#cite_note-SMTnamba-55">[55]</a></sup> While localizing <i>Persona 3</i> for English-speaking countries, the <a href="/wiki/Japanese_honorifics" title="Japanese honorifics">honorifics</a> used by the characters in the original Japanese script were retained. According to Maragos, their use "[added] so much more meaning to the text".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1UP-p4localinterview_53-1"><a href="#cite_note-1UP-p4localinterview-53">[53]</a></sup> In an interview with RPGamer, project editor Yu Namba explained that during the process of translation, some of the Japanese humor, "things that made absolutely no sense in western culture…were replaced with jokes that at least somewhat parallel the originals."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RPGamer-p3interview_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-RPGamer-p3interview-56">[56]</a></sup> One of the changes that needed to be made was to the school tests, which were based around questions on the English language. A similar change was Mitsuru's second language: in the original version it was English, but for the localized version her second language was changed to French. This choice was influenced by her cultured appearance. In addition, in-game references to the original <i><a href="/wiki/Shin_Megami_Tensei" title="Shin Megami Tensei">Shin Megami Tensei</a></i> were altered to references to <i><a href="/wiki/Revelations:_Persona" title="Revelations: Persona">Revelations: Persona</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DesPanel_54-1"><a href="#cite_note-DesPanel-54">[54]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SMTnamba_55-1"><a href="#cite_note-SMTnamba-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shin_Megami_Tensei:_Persona_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The soundtrack for <i>Persona 3</i> was composed entirely by <a href="/wiki/Shoji_Meguro" title="Shoji Meguro">Shoji Meguro</a>, with the sole exception of "Adventured Act", which was composed by Yosuke Uda.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-semo-p3japan_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-semo-p3japan-57">[57]</a></sup> It was released as a two disc soundtrack in Japan by <a href="/wiki/Aniplex" title="Aniplex">Aniplex</a> on July 19, 2006. A selection of tracks from the full soundtrack was bundled with the North American release of the game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-semo-p3us_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-semo-p3us-58">[58]</a></sup> An arranged album, titled <i>Burn My Dread -Reincarnation: Persona 3-</i>, was also released in Japan by Aniplex on April 18, 2007. It contains eleven arrangements of tracks from <i>Persona 3</i>, as well as an extended version of the song "Burn My Dread."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-semo-bmdr_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-semo-bmdr-59">[59]</a></sup> Meguro stated that the development of <i>Persona 3</i> was one of his first opportunities to fully realize his music in video games. The soundtrack features a high use of vocals, though Meguro did not consider this as special or exceptional. A tune from previous <i>Persona</i> titles he rearranged was "Aria of the Soul", the theme of the Velvet Room. The game's battle theme, "Mass Destruction", was originally just a prototype, but the reception to it was so positive that it went into the final game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Persona3Liners_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-Persona3Liners-60">[60]</a></sup> In the past, the hardware limitations of the original <a href="/wiki/PlayStation" title="PlayStation">PlayStation</a> required him to compose music in 100-200 <a href="/wiki/Kilobyte" title="Kilobyte">kilobyte</a> samples, which he felt made the music sound "pretty cheap". The move to the <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_2" title="PlayStation 2">PlayStation 2</a> allowed for real-time <a href="/wiki/Streaming_media" title="Streaming media">streaming</a> of music. Meguro considers this "the point at which [he] was finally able to express [his] music without making any compromises". He was also worried about the pronunciation of the English lyrics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>Meguro returned to compose new music for <i>Persona 3: FES</i>. Released in Japan by Aniplex on May 2, 2007, the soundtrack contained the original score for <i>FES</i>, as well as arrangements of music from earlier games in the <i>Persona</i> series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-semo-fesost_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-semo-fesost-62">[62]</a></sup> "The Snow Queen", composed by Kenichi Tsuchiya, is a remix of the theme in <i><a href="/wiki/Revelations:_Persona" title="Revelations: Persona">Revelations: Persona</a></i>. "Maya's Theme", composed by Kenichi Tsuchiya, and "Time Castle", composed by Toshiko Tasaki, are remixes of tracks from <i><a href="/wiki/Persona_2:_Innocent_Sin" title="Persona 2: Innocent Sin">Persona 2: Innocent Sin</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rpgfan-fesost_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-rpgfan-fesost-63">[63]</a></sup> <i>Persona 3 Portable</i> contains new background music, which can be heard if the player chooses to control the game's new female protagonist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-P3P-Upgrades_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-P3P-Upgrades-64">[64]</a></sup> The game's official soundtrack was released in Japan by Aniplex on November 25, 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Legacy">Legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shin_Megami_Tensei:_Persona_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Persona_3_FES"><i>Persona 3 FES</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shin_Megami_Tensei:_Persona_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Persona 3 FES">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Shin Megami Tensei: Persona 3 FES</i> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">ペルソナ3フェス</span><span class="t_nihongo_comma" style="display:none">,</span> <i>Perusona Surī Fesu</i><sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint"><a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets"><span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">?</span></a></sup>)</span> is an add-on disc for <i>Persona 3</i> containing updates to the original game, as well as a new <a href="/wiki/Epilogue" title="Epilogue">epilogue</a> in which the player controls <a href="/wiki/List_of_Persona_3_characters#Aigis" title="List of Persona 3 characters">Aigis</a>. <i>FES</i> was released in Japan on April 19, 2007, as both a stand-alone game, and with the "director's cut" version of <i>Persona 3</i>. Overseas, the combined edition was published in North America by <a href="/wiki/Atlus#Atlus_USA" title="Atlus">Atlus U.S.A.</a> on April 22, 2008, and in Europe by <a href="/wiki/Koei" title="Koei">Koei</a> on October 17, 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fes-release-info_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-fes-release-info-5">[5]</a></sup> According to the game's director, Katsura Hashino, the subtitle "Fes" is derived from the word "festival".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RPGFan_Persona_3_FES_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-RPGFan_Persona_3_FES-66">[66]</a></sup> This version of the game was re-released as a PS2 Classic on PSN for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PS3" title="PS3">PS3</a> in 2012. Players of the original Persona 3 are given the option of transferring certain data from the original version's save file, such as the player's compendium, social-related stats, and maxed Social Link items.</p>
<p>The expansion to <i>Persona 3</i>, in addition to adding new content to the main game (referred to as "The Journey", or "Episode Yourself" in the Japanese version), includes an epilogue to the original story titled "The Answer" ("Episode Aegis" in the Japanese version). The core gameplay of The Answer is similar to that of The Journey, although the Social Link system has been removed, and the player does not attend school.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gamespot-Persona_3_FES_Review_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gamespot-Persona_3_FES_Review-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Answer">The Answer</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shin_Megami_Tensei:_Persona_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: The Answer">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The events of The Answer begin on March 31, shortly after the end of the original game. During the opening sequence, it is revealed that the Protagonist has died;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> the other characters speculate that his death is related to his defeating Nyx.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> The school year has ended, and the dorm is to be closed down soon. Aigis reveals to the group that she will not be attending school next year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> During their last dinner party, the SEES members discover that they are trapped in their dorm, and that the day March 31 is repeating itself.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gamespot-Persona_3_FES_Review_67-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gamespot-Persona_3_FES_Review-67">[67]</a></sup> Later, a large door-like hole opens in the floor of the dorm, and SEES is attacked by Metis, an anti-shadow weapon similar to Aigis. In the midst of fighting Metis to protect her friends, Aigis's Persona, <a href="/wiki/Athena" title="Athena">Athena</a>, transforms into <a href="/wiki/Orpheus" title="Orpheus">Orpheus</a>, the original Persona of the Protagonist. She also gains the Protagonist's Wild Card ability.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> Aigis is able to subdue Metis, whose actions were an attempt to end the time skip and save Aigis, who she calls her "sister".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>Underneath the dorm is the Abyss of Time, the cause of the time skip. The Abyss contains seven doors, the insides of which contain multi-floor dungeons, similar in design to Tartarus; it is in these areas that the game's combat takes place.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IGN-Persona_3_FES_Review_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-IGN-Persona_3_FES_Review-74">[74]</a></sup> At the top of each dungeon, the characters witness an event from the past of a member of SEES. After seeing several of these <a href="/wiki/Flashback_(narrative)" title="Flashback (narrative)">flashbacks</a>, the characters discern that the event shown in each door relates to how that person had awakened to their Persona.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> At the top of the seventh and final door, SEES fights a Shadow-like version of the Protagonist. After defeating it, each of them obtain a key. By combining the keys, they would be able to end the time skip and leave the dorm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> However, Metis presents SEES with an alternative: instead of unlocking the front door of the dorm, they may also use the keys to travel back in time, to before the fight against Nyx and the death of the Protagonist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> Now unable to agree on how to use the keys, the characters determine that they must fight each other to decide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> Aigis, Fuuka and Metis claim all eight keys, which fuse into the Final Key. After debating on what to do now, they discover a third, new door in the Abyss of Time, which the group uses (without the Final Key) to travel to the moment the Protagonist sealed Nyx from the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup></p>
<p>Metis explains that the purpose of the seal created by the Protagonist was not to seal away Nyx herself (who is not inherently evil), but to prevent humanity's despair from calling out to Nyx and bringing about the Fall once more. The subconscious will of mankind to despair and wish for death constantly rebirths a monster called Erebus that summons Nyx to destroy the world; Metis implies that Erebus's contact with Nyx is what caused the Fall (that was prevented by SEES).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> SEES realizes that the wishes that created Erebus also came from them, and so they fight it, and are able to defeat it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> Mitsuru points out that Erebus will return, as humans will never stop wishing for death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> After breaking the time skip and exiting through the front door of the dorm with the Final Key, Metis, Aigis, and the rest of SEES are summoned to the Velvet Room, much to Igor's (pleasant) surprise.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> It is here they learn of Metis's true origins: that she is a manifestation of a part of Aigis's personality. Distraught over the death of the Protagonist, she no longer wanted to live like a human, and wished to return to being a machine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> However, after being set free from the Abyss of Time, Aigis changes her mind, deciding to continue to attend school, something she had chosen not to do earlier.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Persona_3_Portable"><i>Persona 3 Portable</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shin_Megami_Tensei:_Persona_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Persona 3 Portable">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Shin Megami Tensei: Persona 3 Portable</i> <span style="font-weight: normal">(<span class="t_nihongo_kanji" lang="ja">ペルソナ3 ポータブル</span><span class="t_nihongo_comma" style="display:none">,</span> <i>Perusona Surī Pōtaburu</i><sup class="t_nihongo_help noprint"><a href="/wiki/Help:Installing_Japanese_character_sets" title="Help:Installing Japanese character sets"><span class="t_nihongo_icon" style="color: #00e; font: bold 80% sans-serif; text-decoration: none; padding: 0 .1em;">?</span></a></sup>)</span>, an <a href="/wiki/Video_game_remake" title="Video game remake">enhanced port</a> of <i>Persona 3</i> for the <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_Portable" title="PlayStation Portable">PlayStation Portable</a>, was released in Japan on November 1, 2009,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-P3P-1UP_7-2"><a href="#cite_note-P3P-1UP-7">[7]</a></sup> and released in North America on July 6, 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-P3P-ATLUSUSA_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-P3P-ATLUSUSA-86">[86]</a></sup> It came to most of Europe on 29 April 2011 and the UK on 28 April 2011. The announcement in <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Famits%C5%AB" title="Famitsū">Famitsū</a></i> revealed that the player would have the option to play as a female character. This selection alters some aspects of the story: the first Persona gained by the Protagonist, Orpheus, has a different appearance; Igor's assistant in the Velvet Room, Elizabeth, can be replaced with a male equivalent named Theodore.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Famitsu_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-Famitsu-87">[87]</a></sup> The gender choice also alters some aspects of the Social Link stories. In addition to the new playable character, there are two new <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Difficulty_level" title="Difficulty level">difficulty levels</a> to select from alongside the original game's three. <i>Persona 3 Portable</i> only includes the story of the original <i>Persona 3</i>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> however, general changes have been made to the plot, regardless of character choice.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-P3P-1UP_7-3"><a href="#cite_note-P3P-1UP-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>The game's revised battle system draws on elements added in <i>Persona 3'</i>s successor, <i><a href="/wiki/Shin_Megami_Tensei:_Persona_4" title="Shin Megami Tensei: Persona 4">Persona 4</a></i>. In combat, the player is able to directly control every character, as an alternative to utilizing the game's artificial intelligence. The ability to guard has been added, and allies will take fatal attacks for the Protagonist, preventing his or her death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Famitsu_87-1"><a href="#cite_note-Famitsu-87">[87]</a></sup> Outside of Tartarus, instead of navigating the game world by directly controlling the Protagonist, the player guides an on-screen cursor around an area, allowing interaction with characters and objects. The game includes the voice acting of the original game, although characters are not shown in the world, instead being represented by on-screen portraits. In addition, the anime <a href="/wiki/Cutscene" title="Cutscene">cutscenes</a> seen in the original <i>Persona 3</i> were replaced to feature in-game graphics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-P3P-Upgrades_64-1"><a href="#cite_note-P3P-Upgrades-64">[64]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Shoji_Meguro" title="Shoji Meguro">Shoji Meguro</a> composed 10 new musical tracks for <i>Persona 3 Portable</i>; with the majority of them being written for the female protagonist's playthrough.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-P3P-Upgrades_64-2"><a href="#cite_note-P3P-Upgrades-64">[64]</a></sup> Several <a href="/wiki/Cameo_appearance" title="Cameo appearance">cameos</a> of characters from <i>Persona 4</i> have been added to <i>Persona 3 Portable</i>, including <a href="/wiki/List_of_Persona_4_characters#Yukiko_Amagi" title="List of Persona 4 characters">Yukiko Amagi</a>, a playable character from <i>Persona 4</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> It also features a cameo from Vincent Brooks, the protagonist of <i><a href="/wiki/Catherine_(video_game)" title="Catherine (video game)">Catherine</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Persona_Q:_Shadow_of_the_Labyrinth"><i>Persona Q: Shadow of the Labyrinth</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shin_Megami_Tensei:_Persona_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Persona Q: Shadow of the Labyrinth">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Persona_Q:_Shadow_of_the_Labyrinth" title="Persona Q: Shadow of the Labyrinth">Persona Q: Shadow of the Labyrinth</a></div>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Persona_Q:_Shadow_of_the_Labyrinth" title="Persona Q: Shadow of the Labyrinth">Persona Q: Shadow of the Labyrinth</a></i> is a dungeon crawler RPG developed for the Nintendo 3DS. It features both the characters from <i>Persona 3</i> and the ones from <i>Persona 4</i>, and also includes some gameplay elements from the <i>Etrian Odyssey</i> series. The <i>Persona 3</i> campaign starts two weeks before October 4, so Shinjiro is alive and available as a playable character. Just as SEES prepares to enter Tartarus that night, they are pulled into the Velvet Room and sent to a school they have never seen before. While searching the area they meet the amnesiacs Zen and Rei and the Investigation Team, the latter of whom have also been pulled into the strange school: they must now work together in order to escape. The game was released in Japan on June 5, 2014, North America on November 25, 2014 and Europe on November 28, 2014.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Release">Release</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shin_Megami_Tensei:_Persona_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Release">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>When the original PlayStation 2 version of <i>Persona 3</i> was first released in Japan, it sold 127,472 copies in its first week and 210,319 copies overall in Japan by 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> The North American release of <i>Persona 3</i> shipped as a <a href="/wiki/Special_edition" title="Special edition">collector's edition</a> box, containing the game, a soundtrack disc, and a 52-page art book. The game's original release date was July 24, 2007. However, Atlus encountered a problem with the manufacturing of the art book several days before the intended ship date. Instead of shipping the game without the book, the company decided to push its release back three weeks, to August 14. Atlus issued a press release explaining that they were delaying the game so as maintain the quality of the package, which would have been "irreparably compromised" if they had "revise[d] or abandon[ed] the deluxe package."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Persona 3 FES</i> was first released alongside the original game in two forms: the "Regular Edition" — containing both the "director's cut" version of <i>Persona 3</i>, and the new epilogue — as two separate discs, and the "Append Edition", containing only the epilogue, on a single disc.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rpgamer-p3fesannounce_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-rpgamer-p3fesannounce-94">[94]</a></sup> <i>Persona 3</i> and its expansion were released simultaneously in Japan on April 19, 2007. At the time, Atlus had not announced plans to release <i>FES</i> outside Japan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RPGamer-p3interview_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-RPGamer-p3interview-56">[56]</a></sup> This announcement did not come until February 2008, when the game's North American release date was revealed to be April 22, 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> An exclusive <a href="/wiki/Amazon.com" title="Amazon.com">Amazon.com</a> limited edition bundle was released on November 28, 2008, containing <i>Art of Persona 3</i> artbook, Persona 3 soundtrack disc and the <i>FES</i> edition in a cardboard sleeve.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> The FES edition of the game was also released on PSN on April 10, 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ignpsn_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-ignpsn-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Persona 3 Portable</i> was released as a stand-alone game and as part of a bundle package, which includes a T-shirt and desk calendar.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> The game on its own retails for 6,279 yen (US$68), while the bundle (known as <i>Persona 3 Portable DX</i>) sells for 8,495 yen (US$92).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> In its first month of release, <i>Persona 3 Portable</i> sold over 158,000 copies in Japan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> During the North American release, Atlus offered Junpei's hat as a pre-order bonus for purchasing "Persona 3 Portable".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_reception">Critical reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shin_Megami_Tensei:_Persona_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Critical reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
