<p><i>Persona 3</i> received positive reviews upon its release, earning a Metacritic score of 86.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Metacritic-original_113-1"><a href="#cite_note-Metacritic-original-113">[113]</a></sup> Shane Bettenhausen of <a href="/wiki/1UP.com" title="1UP.com">1UP.com</a> called the game a "refreshingly new take on the <i>MegaTen</i> [<i>Megami Tensei</i>] concept", and "the best RPG hitting the PS2 this year." He praised the "excellent" AI created to direct the actions of party members during battle, which he felt created "the series' speediest and most dynamic battle system to date."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1UP-Persona_3_Review_104-1"><a href="#cite_note-1UP-Persona_3_Review-104">[104]</a></sup> Jeff Haynes from <a href="/wiki/IGN" title="IGN">IGN</a> criticized the system, finding that it would occasionally result in the death of the player's character, which causes a <a href="/wiki/Game_over" title="Game over">game over</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IGN-Persona_3_Review_15-5"><a href="#cite_note-IGN-Persona_3_Review-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>GameTrailers gave the game a score of 9.0, calling it "a rare supernatural delicacy" stating it's an RPG that fans of the genre shouldn't miss out on. <a href="/wiki/GameSpy" title="GameSpy">GameSpy</a>'s Patrick Joynt praised the social elements of <i>Persona 3</i>, calling the game's Social Links "almost universally fascinating." While he suspected the simulation elements would "probably be the biggest hurdle" for fans of role-playing or <i>Megami Tensei</i> games, in his review he wrote that he "can't stress enough how well-done it is."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gamespy-Persona_3_Review_110-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gamespy-Persona_3_Review-110">[110]</a></sup> Heidi Kemps of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GamesRadar" title="GamesRadar">GamesRadar</a> found the game's teenage themes to be "a refreshing change" from those of other games in the genre, as they touch on "the social awkwardness common at that point in life."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GamesRadar-Persona_3_Review_106-1"><a href="#cite_note-GamesRadar-Persona_3_Review-106">[106]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Game_Informer" title="Game Informer">Game Informer</a>'</i>s Joe Juba found the game's environments to be weak, as "most of the game takes place within one tower [Tartarus]." He also in his review noted that the game's roots in the <i>Megami Tensei</i> series would come across as foreign to new players. "If you don’t know anything about fusing Personas, or simply that 'bufu' means 'ice attack,' you have some catching up to do."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GI-Persona_3_FES_Review_107-1"><a href="#cite_note-GI-Persona_3_FES_Review-107">[107]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Persona 3: FES</i> received a score of 89 on Metacritic, slightly higher than that of <i>Persona 3</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Metacritic-fes_114-1"><a href="#cite_note-Metacritic-fes-114">[114]</a></sup> The plot of The Answer provides "much-needed narrative closure" to the story of The Journey, according to Shane Bettenhausen.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1UP-Persona_3_FES_Review_105-1"><a href="#cite_note-1UP-Persona_3_FES_Review-105">[105]</a></sup> Kevin VanOrd called <i>FES</i> a "wonderfully enhanced version of an already-great RPG"; in his review, he recommends the game to new players and those who had already finished the original game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gamespot-Persona_3_FES_Review_67-3"><a href="#cite_note-Gamespot-Persona_3_FES_Review-67">[67]</a></sup> The gameplay of The Answer was criticized by several reviewers for not including the social elements of the original game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gamespot-Persona_3_FES_Review_67-4"><a href="#cite_note-Gamespot-Persona_3_FES_Review-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IGN-Persona_3_FES_Review_74-2"><a href="#cite_note-IGN-Persona_3_FES_Review-74">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gamespy-Persona_3_FES_Review_111-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gamespy-Persona_3_FES_Review-111">[111]</a></sup> VanOrd found the new chapter to be "less interesting" because of this. Jeff Haynes commented that the change "harkens back to a classic, more hardcore RPG experience of fighting and grinding", while done at the expense of what "made <i>Persona 3</i> so intriguing in the first place."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IGN-Persona_3_FES_Review_74-3"><a href="#cite_note-IGN-Persona_3_FES_Review-74">[74]</a></sup> The reviews of GameSpy and IGN reiterated issues found with the original game, such as the inability to directly control party members in battle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IGN-Persona_3_FES_Review_74-4"><a href="#cite_note-IGN-Persona_3_FES_Review-74">[74]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gamespy-Persona_3_FES_Review_111-2"><a href="#cite_note-Gamespy-Persona_3_FES_Review-111">[111]</a></sup></p>
<p>While some critics like <a href="/wiki/IGN" title="IGN">IGN</a> criticized <i>Persona 3 Portable</i> for "losing some of its polish", it was as acclaimed as <i>FES</i>, receiving an 89 out of 100 from <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-metacritic.com_115-1"><a href="#cite_note-metacritic.com-115">[115]</a></sup> making it the third best reviewed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PSP" title="PSP">PSP</a> game on the website.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup> It was praised for, despite having been released twice already, being an adventure worth playing again. This was echoed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GamesRadar" title="GamesRadar">GamesRadar</a>, IGN, <a href="/wiki/1UP.com" title="1UP.com">1UP.com</a> and <i><a href="/wiki/GamePro" title="GamePro">GamePro</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-metacritic.com_115-2"><a href="#cite_note-metacritic.com-115">[115]</a></sup> It received a score of 32/40 from <i><a href="/wiki/Famitsu" title="Famitsu">Famitsu</a></i>; one reviewer wrote that the remake includes "enough differences in the Social Links to make it fun even for old players.",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-p3p-fam-1up_109-1"><a href="#cite_note-p3p-fam-1up-109">[109]</a></sup> and perfect scores from websites such as <a href="/wiki/Destructoid" title="Destructoid">Destructoid</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> and <i>GamePro</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/GameTrailers" title="GameTrailers">GameTrailers</a> went on to nominate the game for "Best PSP Game" in their awards, losing to <i><a href="/wiki/God_of_War:_Ghost_of_Sparta" title="God of War: Ghost of Sparta">God of War: Ghost of Sparta</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> and "Best RPG", losing to <i><a href="/wiki/Mass_Effect_2" title="Mass Effect 2">Mass Effect 2</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> Three websites specific to coverage of RPGs honored it in annual award postings, namely RPGamer (Best Re-release),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> RPGFan (Best Traditional RPG on Handheld),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> and RPGLand (Best Port).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup></p>
<p>Shane Bettenhausen considered the inclusion of Evokers "a ballsy and shocking move" on the part of Atlus, but felt their inclusion created "an edgy sensibitliy that fits perfectly with the overall dark tone" of the game.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1UP-Persona_3_Review_104-2"><a href="#cite_note-1UP-Persona_3_Review-104">[104]</a></sup> Similarly, Joe Juba thought the concept fit "perfectly" with the game's "dark tone".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GI-Persona_3_FES_Review_107-2"><a href="#cite_note-GI-Persona_3_FES_Review-107">[107]</a></sup> Jeff Haynes found the animations of characters using their Evokers to be "intriguing and shocking at the same time".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IGN-Persona_3_Review_15-6"><a href="#cite_note-IGN-Persona_3_Review-15">[15]</a></sup> While previewing <i>Persona 3</i> for GameSpot, Kevin VanOrd said that the continued use of Evokers "never gets old and it never gets any less awesome to watch, and considering that you could play this for fifty, sixty, seventy, eighty hours or more, that's saying something."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> Atlus U.S.A. did not remove the Evokers from <i>Persona 3</i> for its worldwide release, despite the possible controversy. Nich Maragos said on <a href="/wiki/1UP.com" title="1UP.com">1UP.com</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/1UP_Shows_and_Podcasts#Retronauts" title="1UP Shows and Podcasts">Retronauts</a></i> podcast that the company did not receive any criticism for their inclusion, however. "There was never any <a href="/wiki/Jack_Thompson_(activist)" title="Jack Thompson (activist)">Jack Thompson</a>-ing…we didn't get any letters from concerned parents."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Persona 3</i> was named the best role-playing game of 2006 by <i>Famitsu</i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Famitsu-Award_116-1"><a href="#cite_note-Famitsu-Award-116">[116]</a></sup> and of 2007 by GameSpot and RPGFan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GSpot-Award_117-1"><a href="#cite_note-GSpot-Award-117">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RPGFan-Award_120-1"><a href="#cite_note-RPGFan-Award-120">[120]</a></sup> GameSpy gave the title its 2007 PS2 RPG of the Year award and placed it second in the 2007 PS2 Top 10 Games of the Year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GSpy-Award_118-1"><a href="#cite_note-GSpy-Award-118">[118]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup> IGN placed <i>Persona 3 FES</i> fifteenth in their feature "The Top 25 PS2 Games of All Time".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> 1UP.com's 2007 game awards, which ran in the March 2008 issue of <i><a href="/wiki/Electronic_Gaming_Monthly" title="Electronic Gaming Monthly">Electronic Gaming Monthly</a></i>, included <i>Persona 3</i>, given the award for "Most controversial game that created no controversy".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> In 2010, <i>Persona 3</i> ended up coming first place in RPGamer's "Top RPGs of the Decade" list,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RPGamer-Award_119-1"><a href="#cite_note-RPGamer-Award-119">[119]</a></sup> and second place in RPGFan's "Top 20 RPGs of the Past Decade" list behind <i><a href="/wiki/Shin_Megami_Tensei:_Digital_Devil_Saga" title="Shin Megami Tensei: Digital Devil Saga">Shin Megami Tensei: Digital Devil Saga</a></i> &amp; <i><a href="/wiki/Shin_Megami_Tensei:_Digital_Devil_Saga" title="Shin Megami Tensei: Digital Devil Saga">Digital Devil Saga 2</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> According to IGN's Top 100 RPGs of All Time, <i>Persona 3</i> ranks 69th.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shin_Megami_Tensei:_Persona_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Merchandise">Merchandise</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shin_Megami_Tensei:_Persona_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Merchandise">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Several figurines of the characters have been produced by Kotobukiya, a Japanese collectible toy company. They include the Protagonist of the game, Aigis, Mitsuru, and Akihiko.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> The figurines have interchangeable parts, such as an Evoker or weapon, which can be stored in the base. Alter, another Japanese company that specializes in collectibles, has also released 1:8 <a href="/wiki/Scale_model#Terminology" title="Scale model">scale</a> figurines of Elizabeth, Aigis, and Mitsuru.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> The headphones worn by the Protagonist are sold by Audio-Technica, model ATH-EM700(Japan-only version).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> Atlus collaborated with the Japanese publishing company Enterbrain to publish the game's multiple strategy guides and an artbook detailing character and setting designs.</p>
<p>Udon recently announced that they will release an English edition of <a href="/wiki/Enterbrain" title="Enterbrain">Enterbrain</a>'s <i>Persona 3: Official Design Works</i> artbook to be released June 10, 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Manga">Manga</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shin_Megami_Tensei:_Persona_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Manga">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There is also a <a href="/wiki/Manga" title="Manga">manga</a> adaptation of <i>Persona 3</i>, written and illustrated by Shūji Sogabe, and was published monthly in the Japanese magazine <i><a href="/wiki/Dengeki_Maoh" title="Dengeki Maoh">Dengeki Maoh</a></i> until it went on hiatus once <i>Persona 4</i> was released. However, it began serialization again starting November 7, 2011, moving from <i>Dengeki Maoh</i> to Atlus's official <i>Persona Magazine.</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup></p>
<p>As of June 2012, 6 volumes have been released.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Anime">Anime</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shin_Megami_Tensei:_Persona_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Anime">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Persona:_Trinity_Soul" title="Persona: Trinity Soul">Persona: Trinity Soul</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_Persona:_Trinity_Soul_episodes" title="List of Persona: Trinity Soul episodes">list of episodes</a></div>
<p>A non-canonical spin-off <a href="/wiki/Anime" title="Anime">anime</a> to <i>Persona 3</i> titled <i><a href="/wiki/Persona:_Trinity_Soul" title="Persona: Trinity Soul">Persona: Trinity Soul</a></i> aired in Japan starting in January 2008 and ran for twenty-six episodes. Taking place ten years after the events of the game, the anime features Akihiko as a secondary character.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NIS_America" title="NIS America">NIS America</a> licensed the show and released it in two half-season deluxe edition box sets with the original Japanese audio track in 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Films">Films</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shin_Megami_Tensei:_Persona_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Films">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Persona_3_The_Movie:_No._1,_Spring_of_Birth" title="Persona 3 The Movie: No. 1, Spring of Birth">Persona 3 The Movie: No. 1, Spring of Birth</a>; <a href="/wiki/Persona_3_The_Movie:_No._2,_Midsummer_Knight%27s_Dream" title="Persona 3 The Movie: No. 2, Midsummer Knight's Dream">Persona 3 The Movie: No. 2, Midsummer Knight's Dream</a>; <a href="/wiki/Persona_3_The_Movie:_No._3,_Falling_Down" title="Persona 3 The Movie: No. 3, Falling Down">Persona 3 The Movie: No. 3, Falling Down</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Persona_3_The_Movie:_No._4,_Winter_of_Rebirth" title="Persona 3 The Movie: No. 4, Winter of Rebirth">Persona 3 The Movie: No. 4, Winter of Rebirth</a></div>
<p>In June 2012, the end of the newly released <i>Persona 4</i> film announced that <i>Persona 3</i> would receive a film series adaptation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> It is produced by <a href="/wiki/Anime_International_Company" title="Anime International Company">AIC ASTA</a> and directed by Noriaki Akitaya. The main Japanese voice actors from the original game reprised their roles in the film series.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio_drama">Radio drama</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Shin_Megami_Tensei:_Persona_3&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Radio drama">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Several series of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Radio_drama_in_Japan" title="Radio drama in Japan">radio dramas</a> based on <i>Persona 3</i> and <i>Persona 3: FES</i> have been released in Japan. <i>Persona 3 Drama CD: A Certain Day of Summer</i> features an original story voiced by the game's original cast.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dramacd-summer_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-dramacd-summer-149">[149]</a></sup> <i>Persona 3 Drama CD Vol. 2 -Moonlight-</i> links the story of <i>Persona 3</i> and the epilogue released with <i>Persona 3: FES</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dramacd-moon-vol2_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-dramacd-moon-vol2-150">[150]</a></sup> From February to June 2008, a series of character dramas were released as five CDs. The volumes respectively focus on the Protagonist and Ryoji;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dramacd-char-vol1_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-dramacd-char-vol1-151">[151]</a></sup> Junpei and Chidori;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dramacd-char-vol2_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-dramacd-char-vol2-152">[152]</a></sup> Fuuka, Ken, and Aigis;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dramacd-char-vol3_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-dramacd-char-vol3-153">[153]</a></sup> Yukari and Mitsuru;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dramacd-char-vol4_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-dramacd-char-vol4-154">[154]</a></sup> and Akihiko, Shinjiro, and Koromaru.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dramacd-char-vol5_155-0"><a href="#cite_note-dramacd-char-vol5-155">[155]</a></sup> In early 2009, a two-volume side story about Mitsuru was released.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dramacd-newmoon_156-0"><a href="#cite_note-dramacd-newmoon-156">[156]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dramacd-fullmoon_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-dramacd-fullmoon-157">[157]</a></sup></p>

<li id="cite_note-41"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-41">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book"><a href="/wiki/Atlus" title="Atlus">Atlus</a> (2007-08-14). <i>Shin Megami Tensei: Persona 3</i>. <q><b>Aigis:</b> You are... / <b>Yukari:</b> Ryoji-kun...!? / <b>Nyx Avatar:</b> That was my name for a time... I didn't mind it. / <b>Mitsuru:</b> ...What's going on? Wait, are you...? / <b>Nyx Avatar:</b> I am merely a harbinger of the Fall... Although, Nyx and myself are now one in the same.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AShin+Megami+Tensei%3A+Persona+3&amp;rft.au=Atlus&amp;rft.btitle=Shin+Megami+Tensei%3A+Persona+3&amp;rft.date=2007-08-14&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-42"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-42">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book"><a href="/wiki/Atlus" title="Atlus">Atlus</a> (2007-08-14). <i>Shin Megami Tensei: Persona 3</i>. <q><b>Igor:</b> Behold the last power you and I shall unveil... It is the power to bring about a new beginning, or the ultimate end. It may be possible now, with this newfound power... You may be able to defeat the one who cannot be defeated. What you have in your hands is the power of the Universe... Nothing is outside the realm of possibility for you now.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AShin+Megami+Tensei%3A+Persona+3&amp;rft.au=Atlus&amp;rft.btitle=Shin+Megami+Tensei%3A+Persona+3&amp;rft.date=2007-08-14&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-43"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-43">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book"><a href="/wiki/Atlus" title="Atlus">Atlus</a> (2007-08-14). <i>Shin Megami Tensei: Persona 3</i>. <q><b>Aigis:</b> When I thought I might never see you again, something else became clear to me--what I wanted most. My life will be worth living if it's for this reason... Thank you...</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AShin+Megami+Tensei%3A+Persona+3&amp;rft.au=Atlus&amp;rft.btitle=Shin+Megami+Tensei%3A+Persona+3&amp;rft.date=2007-08-14&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
